9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eMany objects hold resources (e.g.: file handles, network connections) which need to be released when their lifetime ends. There are three ways this is handled in modern languages, namely destructors, finalizers, and disposal methods.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eDestructors\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-destructors\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Destructors\" href=\"#destructors\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eDestructors are only used in languages with manual memory management, like C++. There are deterministic rules that govern when destructors are run, so the programmer can ensure \u003cem\u003eall\u003c/em\u003e of them will run, and control \u003cem\u003ewhen\u003c/em\u003e they run. Since the programmer can control when they run, you can use destructors to release critical resources at the right times: e.g., freeing other objects, closing network connections, deleting files, etc.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eHere is an example of destructors in action in C++.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-c++ notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"void doSomeProcessing() {\n   TempFile *t = new TempFile();\n  \n   ...\n \n   if (dont_need_temp_file_anymore()) \n     delete t; // explicit call to a destructor\n  \n   ...\n}\n\nvoid otherFunc() {\n  NetworkConnection n(\u0026quot;www.ucla.edu\u0026quot;);\n\n  ...\n} // destructor for n called when it goes out of scope\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003evoid\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003edoSomeProcessing\u003c/span\u003e() {\n   TempFile *t = \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003enew\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003eTempFile\u003c/span\u003e();\n  \n   ...\n \n   \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eif\u003c/span\u003e (\u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003edont_need_temp_file_anymore\u003c/span\u003e()) \n     \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003edelete\u003c/span\u003e t; \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e//\u003c/span\u003e explicit call to a destructor\u003c/span\u003e\n  \n   ...\n}\n\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003evoid\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003eotherFunc\u003c/span\u003e() {\n  NetworkConnection \u003cspan class=\"pl-smi\"\u003en\u003c/span\u003e(\u003cspan class=\"pl-s\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-pds\"\u003e\"\u003c/span\u003ewww.ucla.edu\u003cspan class=\"pl-pds\"\u003e\"\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/span\u003e);\n\n  ...\n} \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e//\u003c/span\u003e destructor for n called when it goes out of scope\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eFinalizers\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-finalizers\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Finalizers\" href=\"#finalizers\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eIn GC languages, memory is reclaimed automatically by the garbage collector. So finalizers are used to release unmanaged resources like file handles or network connections, which aren't garbage collected. Unlike a destructor, a finalizer may not run at a predictable time or at all, since objects can be garbage collected at any time (or not at all). Since they can't be counted on to run, they're considered a last-line of defense for freeing resources, and often not used at all! We'll learn more about finalizers when we cover Object Oriented Programming.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eHere are some examples of finalizers in Java and Python.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-java notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"// Java finalization example\npublic class SomeClass {\n \n  // called by the garbage collector\n  protected void finalize() throws Throwable\n  {\n    // Free unmanaged resources held by SomeObj \n    ...\n  }\n}\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e// Java finalization example\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003epublic\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eclass\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-smi\"\u003eSomeClass\u003c/span\u003e {\n \n  \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e// called by the garbage collector\u003c/span\u003e\n  \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eprotected\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-smi\"\u003evoid\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003efinalize\u003c/span\u003e() \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003ethrows\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-smi\"\u003eThrowable\u003c/span\u003e\n  {\n    \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e// Free unmanaged resources held by SomeObj \u003c/span\u003e\n    ...\n  }\n}\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"# Python finalizer method\nclass SomeClass :\n  ...\n\n  # called by the garbage collector\n  def __del__(self):\n     # Finalization code goes here\n     ...\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e# Python finalizer method\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eclass\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-v\"\u003eSomeClass\u003c/span\u003e :\n  ...\n\n  \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e# called by the garbage collector\u003c/span\u003e\n  \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003edef\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003e__del__\u003c/span\u003e(\u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003eself\u003c/span\u003e):\n     \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e# Finalization code goes here\u003c/span\u003e\n     ...\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eDisposal methods\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-disposal-methods\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Disposal methods\" href=\"#disposal-methods\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eA disposal method is a function that the programmer must manually call to free non-memory resources (e.g., network connections). You use disposal methods in GC languages because you can't count on a finalizer to run. Disposal provides a guaranteed way to release unmanaged resources when needed. However, we run the risk of forgetting to call the disposal method.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eHere is an example of a disposer in C#.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-cs notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"// C# dispose example\npublic class FontLoader : IDisposable\n{\n  ...\n    \n  public void Dispose()\n  {\n     // do manual disposal here, e.g., free\n     // temp files, close network sockets, etc.\n  }\n}\n\n...\n\nvar f = new FontLoader(...);\n... // use f to draw fonts\nf.Dispose();\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e// C# dispose example\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003epublic\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eclass\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-smi\"\u003eFontLoader\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-smi\"\u003eIDisposable\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-kos\"\u003e{\u003c/span\u003e\n  ..\u003cspan class=\"pl-kos\"\u003e.\u003c/span\u003e\n    \n  \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003epublic\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-smi\"\u003evoid\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003eDispose\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-kos\"\u003e(\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-kos\"\u003e)\u003c/span\u003e\n  \u003cspan class=\"pl-kos\"\u003e{\u003c/span\u003e\n     \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e// do manual disposal here, e.g., free\u003c/span\u003e\n     \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e// temp files, close network sockets, etc.\u003c/span\u003e\n  \u003cspan class=\"pl-kos\"\u003e}\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-kos\"\u003e}\u003c/span\u003e\n\n..\u003cspan class=\"pl-kos\"\u003e.\u003c/span\u003e\n\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-smi\"\u003evar\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003ef\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e=\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003enew\u003c/span\u003e FontLoader\u003cspan class=\"pl-kos\"\u003e(\u003c/span\u003e..\u003cspan class=\"pl-kos\"\u003e.\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-kos\"\u003e)\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-kos\"\u003e;\u003c/span\u003e\n..\u003cspan class=\"pl-kos\"\u003e.\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e// use f to draw fonts\u003c/span\u003e\nf\u003cspan class=\"pl-kos\"\u003e.\u003c/span\u003eDispose\u003cspan class=\"pl-kos\"\u003e(\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-kos\"\u003e)\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-kos\"\u003e;\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-kos\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch2 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eVariable Binding Semantics\u003c/h2\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-variable-binding-semantics\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Variable Binding Semantics\" href=\"#variable-binding-semantics\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eVariable binding semantics\u003c/strong\u003e describe how the name of a variable is related to the memory that stores its value. Turns out, this is \u003cem\u003eharder than you think\u003c/em\u003e!\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eWe'll cover four approaches:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003col dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eValue Semantics\u003c/strong\u003e: a variable is directly bound to storage that holds the value\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eReference Semantics\u003c/strong\u003e: a variable is directly bound to another variable's storage that holds the value\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eObject Reference Semantics\u003c/strong\u003e: a variable is bound to a \u003cem\u003epointer\u003c/em\u003e that points to storage that holds the object/value\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eName Semantics\u003c/strong\u003e: a variable is bound to a \u003cem\u003epointer\u003c/em\u003e that points to an expression graph that evaluates the value\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ol\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eUnlike other concepts in this class, languages often mix-and-match their approaches! For example, C++:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003euses \u003cstrong\u003evalue semantics\u003c/strong\u003e for primitive data types\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003euses \u003cstrong\u003ereference semantics\u003c/strong\u003e with the reference operator (ex: \u003ccode\u003eint \u0026amp;r = x;\u003c/code\u003e)\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003euses \u003cstrong\u003eobject reference semantics\u003c/strong\u003e when explicitly referencing/dereferencing pointers\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eValue Semantics\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-value-semantics\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Value Semantics\" href=\"#value-semantics\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eValue semantics is the simplest approach. Each variable name is directly bound to the storage that represents that variable.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eIn languages like C++ (which uses value semantics for primitive data types), local variables are stored on the stack in an \"activation record\". You can think of an activation record as a map from variable names to their direct values; the entire record lives in memory.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-c++ notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"// activation record: nothing!\nint main() {\n  int x = 5; // activation record: (x,5)\n  int y = 0; // activation record: (x,5), (y,0)\n\n  y = x;     // activation record: (x,5), (y,5)\n}\n// activation record: nothing!\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e//\u003c/span\u003e activation record: nothing!\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eint\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003emain\u003c/span\u003e() {\n  \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eint\u003c/span\u003e x = \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e5\u003c/span\u003e; \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e//\u003c/span\u003e activation record: (x,5)\u003c/span\u003e\n  \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eint\u003c/span\u003e y = \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e0\u003c/span\u003e; \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e//\u003c/span\u003e activation record: (x,5), (y,0)\u003c/span\u003e\n\n  y = x;     \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e//\u003c/span\u003e activation record: (x,5), (y,5)\u003c/span\u003e\n}\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e//\u003c/span\u003e activation record: nothing!\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eWhen reassignment is done, like in the C++ example above, \u003cstrong\u003ethe value is completely copied over\u003c/strong\u003e. After \u003ccode\u003ey = x\u003c/code\u003e, there is no relationship between \u003ccode\u003ey\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003ex\u003c/code\u003e (other than their values being equal). This is distinction may seem obvious, but it's not true for other binding semantics!\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e{: .note }\nThink about how this would work for non-primitive data types. You'd either have to copy over \u003cem\u003eevery\u003c/em\u003e field, which would be expensive, or copy over a pointer - which seems to break the \"copying\" rule. The former is so expensive that most languages do not implement it by default (colloquially, this is called deep copying).\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eReference Semantics\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-reference-semantics\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Reference Semantics\" href=\"#reference-semantics\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eReference semantics\u003c/strong\u003e allows you to assign an \u003cem\u003ealias name\u003c/em\u003e to an existing variable and read/write it through that alias. The reference variable functions identically to the previous variable. Unlike other binding strategies, it's really only relevant when you have \u003cem\u003emultiple\u003c/em\u003e variables.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eTake a look at this C++ example. Recall that in C++, we place an ampersand (\u003ccode\u003e\u0026amp;\u003c/code\u003e) in front of a variable declaration to make it a reference:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-c++ notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"int main() {\n  string role = \u0026quot;SWE\u0026quot;;\n  string \u0026amp;truth = role; // binds truth to role\n\n  truth = \u0026quot;QA\u0026quot;; // since truth points to the same mem location as role, this updates both!\n\n  cout \u0026lt;\u0026lt; \u0026quot;Addr of role: \u0026quot;  \u0026lt;\u0026lt; \u0026amp;role \u0026lt;\u0026lt; endl;\n  cout \u0026lt;\u0026lt; \u0026quot;Addr of truth: \u0026quot; \u0026lt;\u0026lt; \u0026amp;truth \u0026lt;\u0026lt; endl;\n}\n// both role and truth will have the value \u0026quot;QA\u0026quot;\n// the printed addresses will be the same!\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eint\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003emain\u003c/span\u003e() {\n  string role = \u003cspan class=\"pl-s\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-pds\"\u003e\"\u003c/span\u003eSWE\u003cspan class=\"pl-pds\"\u003e\"\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/span\u003e;\n  string \u0026amp;truth = role; \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e//\u003c/span\u003e binds truth to role\u003c/span\u003e\n\n  truth = \u003cspan class=\"pl-s\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-pds\"\u003e\"\u003c/span\u003eQA\u003cspan class=\"pl-pds\"\u003e\"\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/span\u003e; \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e//\u003c/span\u003e since truth points to the same mem location as role, this updates both!\u003c/span\u003e\n\n  cout \u0026lt;\u0026lt; \u003cspan class=\"pl-s\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-pds\"\u003e\"\u003c/span\u003eAddr of role: \u003cspan class=\"pl-pds\"\u003e\"\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/span\u003e  \u0026lt;\u0026lt; \u0026amp;role \u0026lt;\u0026lt; endl;\n  cout \u0026lt;\u0026lt; \u003cspan class=\"pl-s\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-pds\"\u003e\"\u003c/span\u003eAddr of truth: \u003cspan class=\"pl-pds\"\u003e\"\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/span\u003e \u0026lt;\u0026lt; \u0026amp;truth \u0026lt;\u0026lt; endl;\n}\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e//\u003c/span\u003e both role and truth will have the value \"QA\"\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e//\u003c/span\u003e the printed addresses will be the same!\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe key insight is that \u003ccode\u003e\u0026amp;truth\u003c/code\u003e isn't a pointer to the \u003ccode\u003erole\u003c/code\u003e variable; it points to the \u003cstrong\u003esame memory location\u003c/strong\u003e as \u003ccode\u003erole\u003c/code\u003e! When we update \u003ccode\u003etruth\u003c/code\u003e, we also update \u003ccode\u003erole\u003c/code\u003e (and vice-versa).\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eAnother simple example is in the slides:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-c++ notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"int main() {\n  int x = 5;\n  int \u0026amp;r = x;\n  r += 1;\n  // at this point, *both* x and r have the value 6!\n}\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eint\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003emain\u003c/span\u003e() {\n  \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eint\u003c/span\u003e x = \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e5\u003c/span\u003e;\n  \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eint\u003c/span\u003e \u0026amp;r = x;\n  r += \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e1\u003c/span\u003e;\n  \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e//\u003c/span\u003e at this point, *both* x and r have the value 6!\u003c/span\u003e\n}\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eUnder the hood, references are often implemented with pointers - this is how it works in C++!\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e{: .note }\nPhilosophically, you could argue that \"both\" is the wrong word to use - the variable and the reference copy are \u003cem\u003ethe same thing\u003c/em\u003e!\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eObject Reference Semantics\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-object-reference-semantics\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Object Reference Semantics\" href=\"#object-reference-semantics\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eObject reference semantics\u003c/strong\u003e binds a variable name a pointer variable that itself points to an object or value. It's both very common and also a little confusing, so we'll spend a good chunk of time on this one!\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e(unlike reference semantics which hides its use of pointers, with object reference semantics the pointers are explicit and you can read/write them!)\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eLet's take a look at a Python example first. In Python, small integer literals like \u003ccode\u003e5\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003e20\u003c/code\u003e are actually \u003cstrong\u003eallocated on the heap\u003c/strong\u003e; they aren't created and recreated every time a new variable is made. Instead, the activation record maps variables to pointers to items on the heap.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eLet's take a look at what that implies:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"def main():\n  x = 5     # x points to a 5 on the heap!\n  y = 20    # y points to a 20 on the heap!\n  y = x     # y is re-pointed to 5 on the heap; no values are copied!\n            # instead, the *pointer* value for x is copied to y\n            # at this point, the 20 can be garbage collected, since there are no references to it!\n  y = y + 1 # y now points to a 6 on the heap;\n            # x is unchanged!\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003edef\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003emain\u003c/span\u003e():\n  \u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003ex\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e=\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e5\u003c/span\u003e     \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e# x points to a 5 on the heap!\u003c/span\u003e\n  \u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003ey\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e=\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e20\u003c/span\u003e    \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e# y points to a 20 on the heap!\u003c/span\u003e\n  \u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003ey\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e=\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003ex\u003c/span\u003e     \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e# y is re-pointed to 5 on the heap; no values are copied!\u003c/span\u003e\n            \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e# instead, the *pointer* value for x is copied to y\u003c/span\u003e\n            \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e# at this point, the 20 can be garbage collected, since there are no references to it!\u003c/span\u003e\n  \u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003ey\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e=\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003ey\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e+\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e1\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e# y now points to a 6 on the heap;\u003c/span\u003e\n            \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e# x is unchanged!\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThere are two key behaviours to call out:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eon \u003ccode\u003ey = x\u003c/code\u003e, the \u003cstrong\u003epointer values are copied\u003c/strong\u003e, but \u003cstrong\u003enot the memory itself\u003c/strong\u003e.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eon \u003ccode\u003ey = y + 1\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003ex\u003c/code\u003e is unaffected, since we create a new object and change \u003ccode\u003ey\u003c/code\u003e's pointer; not the underlying object!\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eTake a look at a more complicated object with fields:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"class Nerd:\n def __init__(self,name,iq):\n  self.name = name\n  self.iq = iq\n\n def study(self):\n  self.iq = self.iq + 50\n\n def iq(self):\n  return self.iq\n\n def myname(self):\n  return self.name\n\ndef main():\n n1 = Nerd(\u0026quot;Carey\u0026quot;, 100) # points to a Carey nerd on the heap\n n2 = Nerd(\u0026quot;Paul\u0026quot;, 200)  # points to a Paul nerd on the heap\n n2 = n1                 # changes n2 to point to the Carey nerd;\n                         # the Paul nerd can be GC'd!\n n1.study()              # changes the Carey nerd's IQ to 150\n print(f\u0026quot;{n2.myname()}'s IQ is {n2.iq()}\u0026quot;) # n2 points to the Carey Nerd, so \u0026quot;Carey's IQ is 150\u0026quot;!\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eclass\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-v\"\u003eNerd\u003c/span\u003e:\n \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003edef\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003e__init__\u003c/span\u003e(\u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003eself\u003c/span\u003e,\u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003ename\u003c/span\u003e,\u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003eiq\u003c/span\u003e):\n  \u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003eself\u003c/span\u003e.\u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003ename\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e=\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003ename\u003c/span\u003e\n  \u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003eself\u003c/span\u003e.\u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003eiq\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e=\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003eiq\u003c/span\u003e\n\n \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003edef\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003estudy\u003c/span\u003e(\u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003eself\u003c/span\u003e):\n  \u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003eself\u003c/span\u003e.\u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003eiq\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e=\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003eself\u003c/span\u003e.\u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003eiq\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e+\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e50\u003c/span\u003e\n\n \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003edef\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003eiq\u003c/span\u003e(\u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003eself\u003c/span\u003e):\n  \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003ereturn\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003eself\u003c/span\u003e.\u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003eiq\u003c/span\u003e\n\n \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003edef\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003emyname\u003c/span\u003e(\u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003eself\u003c/span\u003e):\n  \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003ereturn\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003eself\u003c/span\u003e.\u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003ename\u003c/span\u003e\n\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003edef\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003emain\u003c/span\u003e():\n \u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003en1\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e=\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-v\"\u003eNerd\u003c/span\u003e(\u003cspan class=\"pl-s\"\u003e\"Carey\"\u003c/span\u003e, \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e100\u003c/span\u003e) \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e# points to a Carey nerd on the heap\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003en2\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e=\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-v\"\u003eNerd\u003c/span\u003e(\u003cspan class=\"pl-s\"\u003e\"Paul\"\u003c/span\u003e, \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e200\u003c/span\u003e)  \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e# points to a Paul nerd on the heap\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003en2\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e=\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003en1\u003c/span\u003e                 \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e# changes n2 to point to the Carey nerd;\u003c/span\u003e\n                         \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e# the Paul nerd can be GC'd!\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003en1\u003c/span\u003e.\u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003estudy\u003c/span\u003e()              \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e# changes the Carey nerd's IQ to 150\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003eprint\u003c/span\u003e(\u003cspan class=\"pl-s\"\u003ef\"\u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-kos\"\u003e{\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003en2\u003c/span\u003e.\u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003emyname\u003c/span\u003e()\u003cspan class=\"pl-kos\"\u003e}\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/span\u003e's IQ is \u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-kos\"\u003e{\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003en2\u003c/span\u003e.\u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003eiq\u003c/span\u003e()\u003cspan class=\"pl-kos\"\u003e}\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\"\u003c/span\u003e) \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e# n2 points to the Carey Nerd, so \"Carey's IQ is 150\"!\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe confusion here is:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003en2 = n1\u003c/code\u003e doesn't change \u003cem\u003eany\u003c/em\u003e underlying objects; it's just a pointer copy\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003ehowever, \u003ccode\u003en1.study()\u003c/code\u003e changes a \u003cstrong\u003efield inside an object\u003c/strong\u003e.\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003ea \u003ccode\u003e150\u003c/code\u003e is put on the heap, and \u003ccode\u003eself.iq\u003c/code\u003e now points to it\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eso, we've changed the field of an object through object reference!\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe difference in how object reference semantics treats object assignment (\u003ccode\u003en2 = n1\u003c/code\u003e) and field access (\u003ccode\u003en1.study()\u003c/code\u003e) is important!\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eWith this in mind: many languages use object reference semantics. Some use it for everything, like Python - others, like Java, only use it for complex objects (and value semantics for primitives).\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch4 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eEquality\u003c/h4\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-equality\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Equality\" href=\"#equality\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eWith object reference semantics, we need to introduce some better tools that test for equality: two pointers with different values could point to the same block of memory!\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eObject Identity\u003c/strong\u003e: Do two object references refer to the same object at the same address in RAM.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eObject Equality\u003c/strong\u003e: Do two object references refer to objects that have equivalent values (even if they're different objects in RAM).\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eSome languages, like Python, have \u003ccode\u003e==\u003c/code\u003e perform object equality by default. Others, like Java, perform object identity - this is why you shouldn't use \u003ccode\u003e==\u003c/code\u003e to compare strings in Java!\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch4 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eC++ Pointers\u003c/h4\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-c-pointers\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: C++ Pointers\" href=\"#c-pointers\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eIn C++, pointers explicitly perform object referencing semantics!\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003ewhen using \u003ccode\u003e*\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003e\u0026amp;\u003c/code\u003e to interact with pointers, we change the underlying values\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003ewithout using \u003ccode\u003e*\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003e\u0026amp;\u003c/code\u003e, we're instead changing the object references!\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-c++ notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"// C++ pointer example\n\nint main() {\n  int x = 5, y = 6;\n  int *px = \u0026amp;x; // pointer to the same memory block as x\n  int *py = \u0026amp;y; // pointer to the same memory block as y\n\n  *py = *px;    // changes the underlying memory, but not the pointers!\n  py = px;      // changes the pointers, but not the underlying memory!\n  *py = 42;     // changes the underlying memory, but not the pointers!\n}\n\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e//\u003c/span\u003e C++ pointer example\u003c/span\u003e\n\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eint\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003emain\u003c/span\u003e() {\n  \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eint\u003c/span\u003e x = \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e5\u003c/span\u003e, y = \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e6\u003c/span\u003e;\n  \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eint\u003c/span\u003e *px = \u0026amp;x; \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e//\u003c/span\u003e pointer to the same memory block as x\u003c/span\u003e\n  \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eint\u003c/span\u003e *py = \u0026amp;y; \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e//\u003c/span\u003e pointer to the same memory block as y\u003c/span\u003e\n\n  *py = *px;    \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e//\u003c/span\u003e changes the underlying memory, but not the pointers!\u003c/span\u003e\n  py = px;      \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e//\u003c/span\u003e changes the pointers, but not the underlying memory!\u003c/span\u003e\n  *py = \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e42\u003c/span\u003e;     \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e//\u003c/span\u003e changes the underlying memory, but not the pointers!\u003c/span\u003e\n}\n\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eIt's helpful to differentiate between the three different binding semantics by the different ways C++ lets you use them!\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eName and Need Semantics\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-name-and-need-semantics\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Name and Need Semantics\" href=\"#name-and-need-semantics\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eName semantics\u003c/strong\u003e binds a variable name to a pointer that points to an expression graph called a \"thunk\".\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e{: .note }\nHere, we mean graph in the computer science sense - nodes connected by edges!\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eConsider the Haskell expression:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-haskell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"square x = x*x\nc = square (a + b)\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003esquare x \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003e=\u003c/span\u003e x\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003e*\u003c/span\u003ex\nc \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003e=\u003c/span\u003e square (a \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003e+\u003c/span\u003e b)\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eWe can draw the following graph to illustrate how the values are related to each other:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003csection class=\"js-render-needs-enrichment render-needs-enrichment position-relative\" data-identity=\"82025fce-9358-4ec1-b8d6-7bde0b04cbad\" data-host=\"https://viewscreen.githubusercontent.com\" data-src=\"https://viewscreen.githubusercontent.com/markdown/mermaid?docs_host=https%3A%2F%2Fdocs.github.com\" data-type=\"mermaid\" aria-label=\"mermaid rendered output container\"\u003e\n  \u003cdiv class=\"js-render-enrichment-target\" data-json=\"{\u0026quot;data\u0026quot;:\u0026quot;graph TD;\\n    c--\u0026amp;gt;square;\\n    square--\u0026amp;gt;+;\\n    +--\u0026amp;gt;a;\\n    +--\u0026amp;gt;b;\\n\u0026quot;}\" data-plain=\"graph TD;\n    c--\u0026gt;square;\n    square--\u0026gt;+;\n    +--\u0026gt;a;\n    +--\u0026gt;b;\n\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n    \u003cdiv class=\"render-plaintext-hidden\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n      \u003cpre lang=\"mermaid\" aria-label=\"Raw mermaid code\"\u003egraph TD;\n    c--\u0026gt;square;\n    square--\u0026gt;+;\n    +--\u0026gt;a;\n    +--\u0026gt;b;\n\u003c/pre\u003e\n    \u003c/div\u003e\n  \u003c/div\u003e\n  \u003cspan class=\"js-render-enrichment-loader d-flex flex-justify-center flex-items-center width-full\" style=\"min-height:100px\" role=\"presentation\"\u003e\n    \u003cspan data-view-component=\"true\"\u003e\n  \u003csvg style=\"box-sizing: content-box; color: var(--color-icon-primary);\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" fill=\"none\" aria-hidden=\"true\" data-view-component=\"true\" class=\"octospinner mx-auto anim-rotate\"\u003e\n    \u003ccircle cx=\"8\" cy=\"8\" r=\"7\" stroke=\"currentColor\" stroke-opacity=\"0.25\" stroke-width=\"2\" vector-effect=\"non-scaling-stroke\" fill=\"none\"\u003e\u003c/circle\u003e\n    \u003cpath d=\"M15 8a7.002 7.002 0 00-7-7\" stroke=\"currentColor\" stroke-width=\"2\" stroke-linecap=\"round\" vector-effect=\"non-scaling-stroke\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\n\u003c/svg\u003e    \u003cspan class=\"sr-only\"\u003eLoading\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003c/span\u003e\n  \u003c/span\u003e\n\u003c/section\u003e\n\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eWhen a variable's value is needed (e.g., to be printed), the expression represented by the graph is \"lazily evaluated\" and a value is produced.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eLanguages like Haskell implement a variant of this called \u003cstrong\u003e\"Need Semantics\"\u003c/strong\u003e which memoize (cache) the result of each evaluation to eliminate redundant computations.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eHere's one example where this memoization can save us computation time:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-haskell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"square x = x*x\nc = square (1 + 2)\nd = square (1 + 2) + 3\ne = square (1 + 2) + 3 + 4\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003esquare x \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003e=\u003c/span\u003e x\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003e*\u003c/span\u003ex\nc \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003e=\u003c/span\u003e square (\u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e1\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003e+\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e2\u003c/span\u003e)\nd \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003e=\u003c/span\u003e square (\u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e1\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003e+\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e2\u003c/span\u003e) \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003e+\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e3\u003c/span\u003e\ne \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003e=\u003c/span\u003e square (\u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e1\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003e+\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e2\u003c/span\u003e) \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003e+\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e3\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003e+\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e4\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eWe can note that there are some redundant computations:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003e1 + 2\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003esquare (1 + 2)\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003esquare (1 + 2) + 3\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eWhen we create an expression graph, there will be \u003cstrong\u003eredundant subgraphs\u003c/strong\u003e. Here are the compact versions of them (think about why they're equivalent!):\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003csection class=\"js-render-needs-enrichment render-needs-enrichment position-relative\" the same thing every time you call them - which is only true if your expressions \u003cstrong\u003ehave no side effects\u003c/strong\u003e, like in Haskell!\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e{: understand:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003ehow functions pass arguments and receive parameters\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003ehow languages return values from functions\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003ehow languages communicate errors across functions\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003ehow functions can be passed as arguments, returned and stored in variables\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003ehow to design functions to operate on a variety of different types of inputs.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch2 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eParameter Passing Semantics\u003c/h2\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-parameter-passing-semantics\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Parameter Passing Semantics\" href=\"#parameter-passing-semantics\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eParameter Passing Semantics is the term we use to describe the underlying mechanisms that languages use to pass arguments (e.g., \u003ccode\u003ex+y\u003c/code\u003e) to functions (e.g., \u003ccode\u003ef(x+y)\u003c/code\u003e).\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe four most common parameter passing semantics are:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003ePass by value: The formal parameter gets a copy of the argument's value/object\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003ePass by reference: The formal parameter is an alias for the argument's value/object\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003ePass by object reference: The formal parameter is a pointer to the argument's value/object\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003ePass by name: The parameter points to an expression graph that represents the argument\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eAs it turns out, these are closely related to binding semantics we learned!\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003ePass by Value\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-pass-by-value\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Pass by Value\" href=\"#pass-by-value\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eApproach: Each argument is first evaluated to get a value, and a \u003cem\u003ecopy\u003c/em\u003e of the value is then passed to the function for local use.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eTake a look at the following C++ program, the parameter \u003ccode\u003en\u003c/code\u003e in \u003ccode\u003estinkify\u003c/code\u003e is passed by value:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-c++ notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"void stinkify(string n) {\n  string t = n + \u0026quot; stinks!\u0026quot;;\n  n = t;\n} \n\nint main() {\n  string s = \u0026quot;Devan\u0026quot;;\n\n  stinkify(s);\n  cout \u0026lt;\u0026lt; s; // Prints \u0026quot;Devan\u0026quot;\n}\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003evoid\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003estinkify\u003c/span\u003e(string n) {\n  string t = n + \u003cspan class=\"pl-s\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-pds\"\u003e\"\u003c/span\u003e stinks!\u003cspan class=\"pl-pds\"\u003e\"\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/span\u003e;\n  n = t;\n} \n\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eint\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003emain\u003c/span\u003e() {\n  string s = \u003cspan class=\"pl-s\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-pds\"\u003e\"\u003c/span\u003eDevan\u003cspan class=\"pl-pds\"\u003e\"\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/span\u003e;\n\n  \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003estinkify\u003c/span\u003e(s);\n  cout \u0026lt;\u0026lt; s; \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e//\u003c/span\u003e Prints \"Devan\"\u003c/span\u003e\n}\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eWhen \u003ccode\u003estinkify(s)\u003c/code\u003e is executed, the \u003ccode\u003en\u003c/code\u003e in \u003ccode\u003estinkify\u003c/code\u003e's activation record is initially copied from \u003ccode\u003es\u003c/code\u003e from \u003ccode\u003emain\u003c/code\u003e. When \u003ccode\u003en\u003c/code\u003e is modified at the end of the function, it only affects the local copy without affecting the original argument \u003ccode\u003es\u003c/code\u003e in main.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003ePass by Reference\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-pass-by-reference\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Pass by Reference\" href=\"#pass-by-reference\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eApproach: \u003cem\u003eSecretly pass the address\u003c/em\u003e of each argument to the function. In the called function, all reads/writes to the parameter are directed to the data at the original address.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eLet's looked at a slightly altered version of above program, where the parameter \u003ccode\u003en\u003c/code\u003e is passed by reference instead (notice the \"\u003ccode\u003e\u0026amp;\u003c/code\u003e\" before \u003ccode\u003en\u003c/code\u003e):\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-c++ notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"void stinkify(string \u0026amp;n) {\n  string t = n + \u0026quot; stinks!\u0026quot;;\n  n = t;\n} \n\nint main() {\n  string s = \u0026quot;Devan\u0026quot;;\n\n  stinkify(s);\n  cout \u0026lt;\u0026lt; s; // Prints \u0026quot;Devan stinks!\u0026quot;\n}\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003evoid\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003estinkify\u003c/span\u003e(string \u0026amp;n) {\n  string t = n + \u003cspan class=\"pl-s\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-pds\"\u003e\"\u003c/span\u003e stinks!\u003cspan class=\"pl-pds\"\u003e\"\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/span\u003e;\n  n = t;\n} \n\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eint\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003emain\u003c/span\u003e() {\n  string s = \u003cspan class=\"pl-s\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-pds\"\u003e\"\u003c/span\u003eDevan\u003cspan class=\"pl-pds\"\u003e\"\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/span\u003e;\n\n  \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003estinkify\u003c/span\u003e(s);\n  cout \u0026lt;\u0026lt; s; \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e//\u003c/span\u003e Prints \"Devan stinks!\"\u003c/span\u003e\n}\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThis time when \u003ccode\u003estinkify(s)\u003c/code\u003e is executed, the \u003ccode\u003en\u003c/code\u003e in \u003ccode\u003estinkify\u003c/code\u003e's activation record points to the \u003ccode\u003es\u003c/code\u003e in \u003ccode\u003emain\u003c/code\u003e's activation record. This enables the formal parameter to act as an alias for the original value/object. Thus, each read/write of the formal parameter is directed to the original variable's storage. So the modification of \u003ccode\u003en\u003c/code\u003e changes the \u003ccode\u003es\u003c/code\u003e in \u003ccode\u003emain\u003c/code\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eOne byproduct that can be caused by pass by reference is \u003cstrong\u003ealiasing\u003c/strong\u003e. It occurs when two parameters unknowingly refer to the same value/object and unintentionally modify it. It can cause subtle and difficult bugs.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-c++ notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"void filter(set\u0026lt;int\u0026gt; \u0026amp;in,\n            set\u0026lt;int\u0026gt; \u0026amp;out) {\n  out.clear();\n  for (auto x: in)\n    if (is_prime(x)) out.insert(x);\n}\n\nint main() {\n  set\u0026lt;int\u0026gt; a;\n  // ... fill up a with #s\n  filter(a, a);\n}\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003evoid\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003efilter\u003c/span\u003e(set\u0026lt;\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eint\u003c/span\u003e\u0026gt; \u0026amp;in,\n            set\u0026lt;\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eint\u003c/span\u003e\u0026gt; \u0026amp;out) {\n  out.\u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003eclear\u003c/span\u003e();\n  \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003efor\u003c/span\u003e (\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eauto\u003c/span\u003e x: in)\n    \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eif\u003c/span\u003e (\u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003eis_prime\u003c/span\u003e(x)) out.\u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003einsert\u003c/span\u003e(x);\n}\n\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eint\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003emain\u003c/span\u003e() {\n  set\u0026lt;\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eint\u003c/span\u003e\u0026gt; a;\n  \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e//\u003c/span\u003e ... fill up a with #s\u003c/span\u003e\n  \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003efilter\u003c/span\u003e(a, a);\n}\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe function \u003ccode\u003efilter\u003c/code\u003e is supposed copy all prime numbers from \u003ccode\u003ein\u003c/code\u003e into \u003ccode\u003eout\u003c/code\u003e. Although it seems to do the job perfectly, problem will occur when \u003ccode\u003ein\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003eout\u003c/code\u003e refer to the same variable, as demonstrated with the call \u003ccode\u003efilter(a, a)\u003c/code\u003e above.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eIn the example, when \u003ccode\u003ein\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003eout\u003c/code\u003e refer to \u003ccode\u003ea\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003eout.clear()\u003c/code\u003e will clear the input \u003ccode\u003ea\u003c/code\u003e before it gets processed. This causes the wrong result to be generated.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003ePass by Object Reference\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-pass-by-object-reference\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Pass by Object Reference\" href=\"#pass-by-object-reference\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eApproach: All values/objects are passed by (copy of the) pointer to the called function. The called function can use the pointer to read/mutate the pointed-to argument.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"class Nerd:\n  def __init__(self, name, iq):\n    self.name = name\n    self.iq = iq\n\n  def study(self):\n    self.iq = self.iq + 50\n\n# ... \n\ndef be_a_nerd(n):\n  n.study();\n\ndef main():\n  a = Nerd(\u0026quot;Alwyn\u0026quot;, 150)\n  be_a_nerd(a);\n  print(a)\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003eiq\u003c/span\u003e):\n    \u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003eself\u003c/span\u003e.\u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003ename\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e=\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003ename\u003c/span\u003e\n    \u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003eself\u003c/span\u003e.\u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003eiq\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e=\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003eiq\u003c/span\u003e\n\n  \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003edef\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003estudy\u003c/span\u003e(\u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003eself\u003c/span\u003e):\n    \u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003eself\u003c/span\u003e.\u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003eiq\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e=\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003eself\u003c/span\u003e.\u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003eiq\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e+\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e50\u003c/span\u003e\n\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e# ... \u003c/span\u003e\n\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003edef\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003ebe_a_nerd\u003c/span\u003e(\u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003en\u003c/span\u003e):\n  \u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003en\u003c/span\u003e.\u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003estudy\u003c/span\u003e();\n\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003edef\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003emain\u003c/span\u003e():\n  \u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003ea\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e=\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-v\"\u003eNerd\u003c/span\u003e(\u003cspan class=\"pl-s\"\u003e\"Alwyn\"\u003c/span\u003e, \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e150\u003c/span\u003e)\n  \u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003ebe_a_nerd\u003c/span\u003e(\u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003ea\u003c/span\u003e);\n  \u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003eprint\u003c/span\u003e(\u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003ea\u003c/span\u003e)\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eIn the python code, the call \u003ccode\u003ebe_a_nerd(a)\u003c/code\u003e copies the object reference \u003ccode\u003ea\u003c/code\u003e into the formal parameter \u003ccode\u003en\u003c/code\u003e of function \u003ccode\u003ebe_a_nerd\u003c/code\u003e. So within \u003ccode\u003ebe_a_nerd\u003c/code\u003e, the local variable n points to our original object, which can be mutated through the object reference.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eBut there is one thing to remember: when we pass by object reference, we can't use assignment to change the value of the original value/object. Let's see the following example:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"def stinkify(n):\n  t = n + \u0026quot; stinks!\u0026quot;;\n  n = t\n\ndef main():\n  s = \u0026quot;Devan\u0026quot;;\n\n  stinkify(s);\n  print(s); # Prints \u0026quot;Devan\u0026quot;\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003edef\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003estinkify\u003c/span\u003e(\u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003en\u003c/span\u003e):\n  \u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003et\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e=\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003en\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e+\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-s\"\u003e\" stinks!\"\u003c/span\u003e;\n  \u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003en\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e=\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003et\u003c/span\u003e\n\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003edef\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003emain\u003c/span\u003e():\n  \u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003es\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e=\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-s\"\u003e\"Devan\"\u003c/span\u003e;\n\n  \u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003estinkify\u003c/span\u003e(\u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003es\u003c/span\u003e);\n  \u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003eprint\u003c/span\u003e(\u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003es\u003c/span\u003e); \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e# Prints \"Devan\"\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eWe might expect the assignment \u003ccode\u003en = t\u003c/code\u003e to change the original variable \u003ccode\u003es\u003c/code\u003e in the calling function. But in fact, the assignment only changes the \u003cem\u003elocal\u003c/em\u003e object reference \u003ccode\u003en\u003c/code\u003e to point to the storage of \u003ccode\u003et\u003c/code\u003e in Heap Memory. It has no imact on the original object reference \u003ccode\u003es\u003c/code\u003e or the object \u003ccode\u003es\u003c/code\u003e points to.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe takeaway is that assignments of object references never change the passed-in value/object. They just change where the local object reference points to. It contrasts with passing by reference, where assignment can change the original value.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eSo, in a language that uses Object References like Java or Python, your function can either return a new object with relevant changes (e.g., \u003ccode\u003ex = stinkify(x)\u003c/code\u003e), or use mutator functions.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003ePass by Name/Need\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-pass-by-nameneed\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Pass by Name/Need\" href=\"#pass-by-nameneed\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eApproach: Each parameter is bound to a pointer that points to an expression graph (a \"thunk\") which can be used to compute the passed-in argument's value.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eHere, a trunk is typically implemented as a lambda function, which can be called to evaluate the full expression graph and produce a concrete result when it is needed.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eHaskell is a notable example of pass by need.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-haskell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"func2 y =\n  y^2+7\n\nfunc1 x =\n  func2 (3 + x)\n\nmain = do\n  let z = func1 5\n  print z\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003efunc2 y \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003e=\u003c/span\u003e\n  y\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003e^\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e2\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003e+\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e7\u003c/span\u003e\n\nfunc1 x \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003e=\u003c/span\u003e\n  func2 (\u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e3\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003e+\u003c/span\u003e x)\n\nmain \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003e=\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003edo\u003c/span\u003e\n  \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003elet\u003c/span\u003e z \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003e=\u003c/span\u003e func1 \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e5\u003c/span\u003e\n  \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003eprint\u003c/span\u003e z\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eIn pass-by-need, once an expression graph is evaluated, the computed result is \u003cem\u003ememoized\u003c/em\u003e (cached) to prevent repeat computation. For example, in the code above, if we do another \u003ccode\u003eprint z\u003c/code\u003e after the existing print, the value of \u003ccode\u003ez\u003c/code\u003e will be cached without the need for another evaluation.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eParameter Passing by Language\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-parameter-passing-by-language\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Parameter Passing by Language\" href=\"#parameter-passing-by-language\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5
